For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/GE_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="GE (disambiguation)">GE (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with the former British <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Company_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="General Electric Company plc">General Electric Company plc</a> (GEC).</div>

<table class="box-Merge_from plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">It has been suggested that <i><a href="/wiki/GE_Industrial" title="GE Industrial">GE Industrial</a></i> be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Merging" title="Wikipedia:Merging">merged</a> into this article. (<a href="/wiki/Talk:General_Electric#Proposed_merge_with_GE_Industrial" title="Talk:General Electric">Discuss</a>)<small><i> Proposed since January 2020.</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>General Electric Company</b> (<b>GE</b>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">conglomerate</a> incorporated in New York City and headquartered in Boston. As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the company operates through the following segments: <a href="/wiki/GE_Aviation" title="GE Aviation">aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/GE_Healthcare" title="GE Healthcare">healthcare</a>, <a href="/wiki/GE_Power" title="GE Power">power</a>, <a href="/wiki/GE_Renewable_Energy" title="GE Renewable Energy">renewable energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/GE_Digital" title="GE Digital">digital industry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Additive_manufacturing" class="mw-redirect" title="Additive manufacturing">additive manufacturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/GE_Capital" title="GE Capital">venture capital and finance</a> and <a href="/wiki/GE_Lighting" title="GE Lighting">lighting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dismantle_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dismantle-3">[3]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" Lighting</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/GE_Power" title="GE Power">GE Power</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/GE_Renewable_Energy" title="GE Renewable Energy">GE Renewable Energy</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/GE_Ventures" title="GE Ventures">GE Ventures</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ge.com/">GE.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>In 2018, GE ranked among the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> as the 18th-largest firm in the U.S. by <a href="/wiki/Gross_revenue" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross revenue">gross revenue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>  In 2011, GE ranked among the Fortune 20 as the 14th-most profitable company but has since very severely underperformed the market (by about 75%) as its profitability collapsed.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_500:_IBM_profit_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_500:_IBM_profit-7">[7]</a></sup> Two employees of GE—<a href="/wiki/Irving_Langmuir" title="Irving Langmuir">Irving Langmuir</a> (1932) and <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Giaever" title="Ivar Giaever">Ivar Giaever</a> (1973)—have been awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_timeline" title="General Electric timeline">General Electric timeline</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation">Formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Formation" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Electric_Shops,_Schenectady,_NY,_aerial_view,_1896.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_aerial_view%2C_1896.jpg/220px-General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_aerial_view%2C_1896.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2638" data-file-height="1719"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 143px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_aerial_view%2C_1896.jpg/220px-General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_aerial_view%2C_1896.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="143" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Electric_Shops,_Schenectady,_NY,_aerial_view,_1896.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General Electric in Schenectady, NY, aerial view, 1896</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Electric_Shops,_Schenectady,_NY,_1896.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_1896.jpg/220px-General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_1896.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2608" data-file-height="1779"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 150px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_1896.jpg/220px-General_Electric_Shops%2C_Schenectady%2C_NY%2C_1896.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="150" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Electric_Shops,_Schenectady,_NY,_1896.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plan of Schenectady plant, 1896<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:570_Lexington_Avenue_(General_Electric_Building)_001.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/570_Lexington_Avenue_%28General_Electric_Building%29_001.jpg/170px-570_Lexington_Avenue_%28General_Electric_Building%29_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 227px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/570_Lexington_Avenue_%28General_Electric_Building%29_001.jpg/170px-570_Lexington_Avenue_%28General_Electric_Building%29_001.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="227" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:570_Lexington_Avenue_(General_Electric_Building)_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Building" title="General Electric Building">General Electric Building</a> at 570 Lexington Avenue, New York</div></div></div>
<p>During 1889, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a> had business interests in many electricity-related companies including <i>Edison Lamp Company</i>, a lamp manufacturer in <a href="/wiki/East_Newark,_New_Jersey" title="East Newark, New Jersey">East Newark, New Jersey</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Edison_Machine_Works" title="Edison Machine Works">Edison Machine Works</a></i>, a manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Dynamo" title="Dynamo">dynamos</a> and large <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motors</a> in <a href="/wiki/Schenectady,_New_York" title="Schenectady, New York">Schenectady, New York</a>; <i>Bergmann &amp; Company</i>, a manufacturer of electric <a href="/wiki/Light_fixture" title="Light fixture">lighting fixtures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lightbulb_socket" title="Lightbulb socket">sockets</a>, and other electric lighting devices; and <i>Edison Electric Light Company</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patent</a>-holding company and the financial arm backed by <a href="/wiki/J._P._Morgan" title="J. P. Morgan">J. P. Morgan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_family" title="Vanderbilt family">Vanderbilt family</a> for Edison's lighting experiments.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>In 1889, <a href="/wiki/Drexel,_Morgan_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Drexel, Morgan &amp; Co.">Drexel, Morgan &amp; Co.</a>, a company founded by J.P. Morgan and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_J._Drexel" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthony J. Drexel">Anthony J. Drexel</a>, financed Edison's research and helped merge those companies under one corporation to form <i>Edison General Electric Company</i>, which was incorporated in New York on April 24, 1889. The new company also acquired <a href="/wiki/Sprague_Electric_Railway_%26_Motor_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprague Electric Railway &amp; Motor Company">Sprague Electric Railway &amp; Motor Company</a> in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jpmorgan_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpmorgan-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>In 1880, Gerald Waldo Hart formed the American Electric Company of <a href="/wiki/New_Britain,_Connecticut" title="New Britain, Connecticut">New Britain, Connecticut</a>, which merged a few years later with <a href="/wiki/Thomson-Houston_Electric_Company" title="Thomson-Houston Electric Company">Thomson-Houston Electric Company</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Charles_A._Coffin" title="Charles A. Coffin">Charles Coffin</a>. In 1887, Hart left to become superintendent of the Edison Electric Company of <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City, Missouri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> General Electric was formed through the 1892 merger of Edison General Electric Company of Schenectady, New York, and Thomson-Houston Electric Company of <a href="/wiki/Lynn,_Massachusetts" title="Lynn, Massachusetts">Lynn, Massachusetts</a>, with the support of Drexel, Morgan &amp; Co.<sup id="cite_ref-jpmorgan_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpmorgan-12">[12]</a></sup> Both plants continue to operate under the GE banner to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The company was incorporated in New York, with the Schenectady plant used as headquarters for many years thereafter. Around the same time, General Electric's Canadian counterpart, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_General_Electric" title="Canadian General Electric">Canadian General Electric</a>, was formed.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>In 1893 General Electric bought the business of Rudolf Eickemeyer in <a href="/wiki/Yonkers,_New_York" title="Yonkers, New York">Yonkers, New York</a>, along with all of its patents and designs. One of the employees was <a href="/wiki/Charles_Proteus_Steinmetz" title="Charles Proteus Steinmetz">Charles Proteus Steinmetz</a>. Only recently arrived in the United States, Steinmetz was already publishing in the field of magnetic hysteresis and had earned worldwide professional recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-IEEEPER_(1996)_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEEEPER_(1996)-16">[16]</a></sup>  Led by Steinmetz, Eickemeyer's firm had developed <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformers</a> for use in the <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">transmission of electrical power</a> among many other mechanical and electrical devices. Steinmetz quickly became known as the engineering wizard in GE's engineering community.<sup id="cite_ref-IEEEPER_(1996)_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEEEPER_(1996)-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_company">Public company</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Public company" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1896, General Electric was one of the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average#History" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">original 12</a> companies listed on the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> where it remained a part of the index for 122 years, though not continuously.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carmen_Miranda_by_General_Electric_(1945).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="1945 magazine ad for an FM radio with pictures of Miranda" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Carmen_Miranda_by_General_Electric_%281945%29.jpg/190px-Carmen_Miranda_by_General_Electric_%281945%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="253" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1240" data-file-height="1650"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 190px;height: 253px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Carmen_Miranda_by_General_Electric_%281945%29.jpg/190px-Carmen_Miranda_by_General_Electric_%281945%29.jpg" data-alt="1945 magazine ad for an FM radio with pictures of Miranda" data-width="190" data-height="253" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carmen_Miranda_by_General_Electric_(1945).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Carmen_Miranda" title="Carmen Miranda">Carmen Miranda</a> in a 1945 advertisement for a General Electric FM radio in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Saturday_Evening_Post" title="The Saturday Evening Post">The Saturday Evening Post</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>In 1911, General Electric absorbed the National Electric Lamp Association (NELA) into its lighting business. GE established its lighting division headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Nela_Park" title="Nela Park">Nela Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Cleveland,_Ohio" title="East Cleveland, Ohio">East Cleveland, Ohio</a>. The lighting division has since remained in the same location.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="RCA_and_NBC">RCA and NBC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: RCA and NBC" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Owen D. Young, through GE, founded the <a href="/wiki/Radio_Corporation_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Corporation of America">Radio Corporation of America</a> (RCA) in 1919, after purchasing the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Wireless_Telegraph_Company_of_America" title="Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company of America">Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company of America</a>. He aimed to expand international radio communications. GE used RCA as its retail arm for radio sales.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1926, RCA co-founded the <a href="/wiki/National_Broadcasting_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="National Broadcasting Company">National Broadcasting Company</a> (NBC), which built two radio broadcasting networks. In 1930, General Electric was charged with antitrust violations and decided to divest itself of RCA.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Television" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1927, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Alexanderson" title="Ernst Alexanderson">Ernst Alexanderson</a> of GE made the first demonstration of his television broadcasts<sup id="cite_ref-inventors.about.com_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventors.about.com-22">[22]</a></sup> at his <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Realty_Plot" title="General Electric Realty Plot">General Electric Realty Plot</a> home at 1132 Adams Rd, Schenectady, New York.  On January 13, 1928, he made what was said to be the first broadcast to the public in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-inventors.about.com_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventors.about.com-22">[22]</a></sup> on GE's <a href="/wiki/W2XAD" class="mw-redirect" title="W2XAD">W2XAD</a>: the pictures were picked up on 1.5 square inch (9.7 square centimeter) screens in the homes of four GE executives. The sound was broadcast on GE's <a href="/wiki/WGY_(AM)" title="WGY (AM)">WGY (AM)</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Experimental television station W2XAD evolved into station <a href="/wiki/WRGB" title="WRGB">WRGB</a> which, along with WGY and WGFM (now <a href="/wiki/WRVE" title="WRVE">WRVE</a>), was owned and operated by General Electric until 1983.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_generation">Power generation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Power generation" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/GE_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="GE Energy">GE Energy</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/GE_Wind_Energy" title="GE Wind Energy">GE Wind Energy</a></div>
<p>Led by <a href="/wiki/Sanford_Alexander_Moss" title="Sanford Alexander Moss">Sanford Alexander Moss</a>, GE moved into the new field of aircraft <a href="/wiki/Turbosupercharger" class="mw-redirect" title="Turbosupercharger">turbo superchargers</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> GE introduced the first set of superchargers during World War I, and continued to develop them during the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a>. Superchargers became indispensable in the years immediately prior to World War II. GE supplied 300,000 turbo superchargers for use in fighter and bomber engines. This work led the U.S. Army Air Corps to select GE to develop the nation's first jet engine during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> This experience, in turn, made GE a natural selection to develop the <a href="/wiki/Whittle_W.1" class="mw-redirect" title="Whittle W.1">Whittle W.1</a> <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">jet engine</a> that was demonstrated in the United States in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> GE was ranked ninth among United States corporations in the value of wartime production contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Although, their early work with Whittle's designs was later handed to <a href="/wiki/Allison_Engine_Company" title="Allison Engine Company">Allison Engine Company</a>. GE <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">Aviation</a> then emerged as one of the world's largest engine manufacturers, bypassing the British company, <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce plc">Rolls-Royce plc</a>.
</p><p>Some consumers <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycotted</a> GE light bulbs, refrigerators and other products during the 1980s and 1990s. The purpose of the boycott was to protest against GE's role in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> production.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>In 2002, GE acquired the wind power assets of Enron during its bankruptcy proceedings.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_Wire_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Wire-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Enron_Wind" title="Enron Wind">Enron Wind</a> was the only surviving U.S. manufacturer of large wind turbines at the time, and GE increased engineering and supplies for the Wind Division and doubled the annual sales to $1.2 billion in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-ieGE_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ieGE-28">[28]</a></sup> It acquired <a href="/wiki/ScanWind" title="ScanWind">ScanWind</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018, GE Power garnered press attention when a model 7HA gas turbine in Texas was shut down for two months due to the break of a <a href="/wiki/Turbine_blade" title="Turbine blade">turbine blade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> This model uses similar blade technology to GE's newest and most efficient model, the 9HA. After the break, GE developed new protective coatings and heat treatment methods. Gas turbines represent a significant portion of GE Power's revenue, and also represent a significant portion of the power generation fleet of several utility companies in the United States. <a href="/wiki/Chubu_Electric" class="mw-redirect" title="Chubu Electric">Chubu Electric</a> of Japan and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lectricit%C3%A9_de_France" title="Électricité de France">Électricité de France</a> also had units that were impacted. Initially, GE did not realize the turbine blade issue of the 9FB unit would impact the new HA units.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Computing">Computing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Computing" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22General+Electric%22">"General Electric"</a> – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22General+Electric%22+-wikipedia">news</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22General+Electric%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22General+Electric%22+-wikipedia">books</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22General+Electric%22">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22General+Electric%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>GE was one of the eight major computer companies of the 1960s along with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burroughs_Corporation" title="Burroughs Corporation">Burroughs</a>, <a href="/wiki/NCR_Corporation" title="NCR Corporation">NCR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Control_Data_Corporation" title="Control Data Corporation">Control Data Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>, <a href="/wiki/RCA" title="RCA">RCA</a> and <a href="/wiki/UNIVAC" title="UNIVAC">UNIVAC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guston_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guston-33">[33]</a></sup> GE had a line of general purpose and special purpose computers, including the <a href="/wiki/GE-200_series" title="GE-200 series">GE 200</a>, <a href="/wiki/GE-400_series" title="GE-400 series">GE 400</a>, and <a href="/wiki/GE-600_series" title="GE-600 series">GE 600</a> series general purpose computers,<sup id="cite_ref-Guston_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guston-33">[33]</a></sup> the GE 4010, GE 4020, and GE 4060 <a href="/wiki/Real-time_computing" title="Real-time computing">real-time</a> <a href="/wiki/Process_control" title="Process control">process control</a> computers, and the <a href="/wiki/DATANET-30" title="DATANET-30">DATANET-30</a> and Datanet 355 message switching computers (DATANET-30 and 355 were also used as front end processors for GE mainframe computers). A Datanet 500 computer was designed, but never sold.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p><p>In 1962, GE started developing its <a href="/wiki/GECOS" class="mw-redirect" title="GECOS">GECOS</a> (later renamed GCOS) <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a>, originally for <a href="/wiki/Batch_processing" title="Batch processing">batch processing</a>, but later extended to <a href="/wiki/Timesharing" class="mw-redirect" title="Timesharing">timesharing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transaction_processing" title="Transaction processing">transaction processing</a>. Versions of GCOS are still in use today. From 1964 to 1969, GE and <a href="/wiki/Bell_Laboratories" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell Laboratories">Bell Laboratories</a> (which soon dropped out) joined with <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a> to develop the <a href="/wiki/Multics" title="Multics">Multics</a> operating system on the <a href="/wiki/GE_645" title="GE 645">GE 645</a> mainframe computer. The project took longer than expected and was not a major commercial success, but it demonstrated concepts such as <a href="/wiki/Single_level_store" class="mw-redirect" title="Single level store">single level store</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_linking" class="mw-redirect" title="Dynamic linking">dynamic linking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hierarchical_file_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Hierarchical file system">hierarchical file system</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ring_(computer_security)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ring (computer security)">ring-oriented security</a>. Active development of Multics continued until 1985.
</p><p>GE got into computer manufacturing because in the 1950s they were the largest user of computers outside the <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="United States federal government">United States federal government</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Guston_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guston-33">[33]</a></sup> aside from being the first business in the world to own a computer. Its major appliance manufacturing plant "<a href="/wiki/GE_Consumer_%26_Industrial" class="mw-redirect" title="GE Consumer &amp; Industrial">Appliance Park</a>" was the first non-governmental site to host one.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> However, in 1970, GE sold its computer division to <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>, exiting the computer manufacturing industry,<sup id="cite_ref-Guston_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guston-33">[33]</a></sup> though it retained its timesharing operations for some years afterwards. GE was a major provider of computer <a href="/wiki/Timesharing" class="mw-redirect" title="Timesharing">time-sharing</a> services, through General Electric Information Services (GEIS, now GXS), offering online computing services that included <a href="/wiki/GEnie" title="GEnie">GEnie</a>.
</p><p>In 2000, when United Technologies Corp. planned to buy Honeywell, GE made a counter-offer that was approved by Honeywell.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> On July 3, 2001, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> issued a statement that "prohibit the proposed acquisition by General Electric Co. of Honeywell Inc.".<sup id="cite_ref-EU-GE-Honeywell_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU-GE-Honeywell-37">[37]</a></sup> The reasons given were it "would create or strengthen dominant positions on several markets and that the remedies proposed by GE were insufficient to resolve the competition concerns resulting from the proposed acquisition of Honeywell".<sup id="cite_ref-EU-GE-Honeywell_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU-GE-Honeywell-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>On June 27, 2014, GE partnered with collaborative design company Quirky to announce its connected LED bulb called Link. The Link bulb is designed to communicate with smartphones and tablets using a mobile app called <a href="/wiki/Wink_(platform)" title="Wink (platform)">Wink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GE,_Global_Operations_Center_-_Cincinnati.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/GE%2C_Global_Operations_Center_-_Cincinnati.jpg/220px-GE%2C_Global_Operations_Center_-_Cincinnati.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5568" data-file-height="3712"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/GE%2C_Global_Operations_Center_-_Cincinnati.jpg/220px-GE%2C_Global_Operations_Center_-_Cincinnati.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GE,_Global_Operations_Center_-_Cincinnati.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GE Global Operations Center in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cincinnati" title="Downtown Cincinnati">Downtown Cincinnati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a></div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions_and_divestments">Acquisitions and divestments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Acquisitions and divestments" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_timeline" title="General Electric timeline">General Electric timeline</a></div>
<p>In December 1985, GE reacquired RCA, primarily for the <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> television network (also parent of <a href="/wiki/Telemundo_Communications_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Telemundo Communications Group">Telemundo Communications Group</a>) for $6.28 billion; this merger surpassed the <a href="/wiki/Capital_Cities/ABC" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital Cities/ABC">Capital Cities/ABC</a> merger that happened earlier that year as the largest non-oil merger in world business history.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The remainder was sold to various companies, including <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann" title="Bertelsmann">Bertelsmann</a> (Bertelsmann acquired <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Thomson_SA" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomson SA">Thomson SA</a>, which traces its roots to Thomson-Houston, one of the original components of GE.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Also in 1986, <a href="/wiki/Kidder,_Peabody_%26_Co." title="Kidder, Peabody &amp; Co.">Kidder, Peabody &amp; Co.</a>, a U.S.-based securities firm, was sold to GE and following heavy losses was sold to <a href="/wiki/PaineWebber" class="mw-redirect" title="PaineWebber">PaineWebber</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Partners" title="Francisco Partners">Francisco Partners</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwest_Venture_Partners" title="Norwest Venture Partners">Norwest Venture Partners</a> acquired a division of GE called GE Information Systems (GEIS). The new company, named <a href="/wiki/GXS_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="GXS (company)">GXS</a>, is based in <a href="/wiki/Gaithersburg,_Maryland" title="Gaithersburg, Maryland">Gaithersburg, Maryland</a>. GXS is a provider of B2B e-Commerce solutions. GE maintains a minority stake in GXS.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Also in 2002, <a href="/wiki/GE_Wind_Energy" title="GE Wind Energy">GE Wind Energy</a> was formed when GE bought the <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbine</a> manufacturing assets of Enron Wind after the <a href="/wiki/Enron_scandal" title="Enron scandal">Enron scandals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_Wire_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Wire-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ieGE_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ieGE-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-desertsky_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-desertsky-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>In 2004, GE bought 80% of <a href="/wiki/Universal_Pictures" title="Universal Pictures">Universal Pictures</a> from <a href="/wiki/Vivendi" title="Vivendi">Vivendi</a>. Vivendi bought 20% of NBC forming the company <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a>. GE then owned 80% of NBCUniversal and Vivendi owned 20%. In 2004, GE completed the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">spin-off</a> of most of its <a href="/wiki/Mortgage_loan" title="Mortgage loan">mortgage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Life_insurance" title="Life insurance">life insurance</a> assets into an independent company, <a href="/wiki/Genworth_Financial" title="Genworth Financial">Genworth Financial</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond, Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Genpact" title="Genpact">Genpact</a> formerly known as GE Capital International Services (GECIS) was established by GE in late 1997 as its captive India-based <a href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" class="mw-redirect" title="Business process outsourcing">BPO</a>. GE sold 60% stake in Genpact to General Atlantic and Oak Hill Capital Partners in 2005 and hived off Genpact into an independent business. GE is still a major client to Genpact today, for services in customer service, finance, information technology and analytics.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In May 2007, GE acquired <a href="/wiki/Smiths_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Smiths Aerospace">Smiths Aerospace</a> for $4.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Also in 2007, GE Oil &amp; Gas acquired Vetco Gray for $1.9 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> followed by the acquisition of Hydril Pressure &amp; Control in 2008 for $1.1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p><p>GE Plastics was sold in 2008 to <a href="/wiki/SABIC" title="SABIC">SABIC</a> (Saudi Arabia Basic Industries Corporation). In May 2008, GE announced it was exploring options for divesting the bulk of its consumer and industrial business. <sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>On December 3, 2009, it was announced that NBCUniversal would become a joint venture between GE and cable television operator <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a>. Comcast would hold a controlling interest in the company, while GE would retain a 49% stake and would buy out shares owned by Vivendi.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>Vivendi would sell its 20% stake in NBCUniversal to GE for US$5.8 billion. Vivendi would sell 7.66% of NBCUniversal to GE for US$2 billion if the GE/Comcast deal was not completed by September 2010 and then sell the remaining 12.34% stake of NBCUniversal to GE for US$3.8 billion when the deal was completed or to the public via an <a href="/wiki/Initial_Public_Offering" class="mw-redirect" title="Initial Public Offering">IPO</a> if the deal was not completed.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>On March 1, 2010, GE announced plans to sell its 20.85% stake in Turkey-based Garanti Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In August 2010, GE Healthcare signed a strategic partnership to bring cardiovascular Computed Tomography (CT) technology from start-up Arineta Ltd. of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> to the hospital market.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In October 2010, GE acquired gas engines manufacture <a href="/wiki/Dresser_Industries" title="Dresser Industries">Dresser Inc.</a> in a $3 billion deal and also bought a $1.6 billion portfolio of retail credit cards from <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ge-in-russia_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ge-in-russia-56">[56]</a></sup> On October 14, 2010, GE announced the acquisition of data migration &amp; SCADA simulation specialists Opal Software.<sup id="cite_ref-htanna_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-htanna-57">[57]</a></sup> In December 2010, for the second time that year (after the Dresser acquisition), GE bought the oil sector company British Wellstream Holding Plc., an oil pipe maker, for 800 million pounds ($1.3 billion).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2011, GE announced that it had completed the acquisition of privately held Lineage Power Holdings, Inc., from The Gores Group, LLC.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In April 2011, GE announced it had completed its purchase of John Wood Plc's Well Support Division for $2.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, GE Capital sold its $2 billion Mexican assets to <a href="/wiki/Santander_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander Group">Santander</a> for $162 million and exit the business in Mexico. Santander additionally assumed the portfolio debts of GE Capital in the country. Following this, GE Capital focused in its core business and shed its non-core assets.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2012, CEO and President of GE Jeff Immelt said that the company would invest <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee_sign" title="Indian rupee sign">₹</a>3 <a href="/wiki/Billion" title="Billion">billion</a>  to accelerate its businesses in <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In October 2012, GE acquired $7 billion worth of bank deposits from <a href="/wiki/Metlife" class="mw-redirect" title="Metlife">Metlife Inc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p><p>On March 19, 2013, Comcast bought GE's shares in NBCU for $16.7 billion, ending the company's longtime stake in television and film media.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2013, GE acquired oilfield pump maker <a href="/wiki/Lufkin_Industries" title="Lufkin Industries">Lufkin Industries</a> for $2.98 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2014, it was announced that GE was in talks to acquire the global power division of French engineering group <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a> for a figure of around $13 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> A rival joint bid was submitted in June 2014 by <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Heavy_Industries" title="Mitsubishi Heavy Industries">Mitsubishi Heavy Industries</a> (MHI) with Siemens seeking to acquire Alstom's gas turbine business for €3.9 billion, and MHI proposing a joint venture in steam turbines, plus a €3.1 billion cash investment. In June 2014 a formal offer from GE worth $17 billion was agreed by the Alstom board. Part of the transaction involved the French government taking a 20% stake in Alstom to help secure France's energy and transport interests and French jobs. A rival offer from Siemens-Mitsubishi Heavy Industries was rejected. The acquisition was expected to be completed in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-AlstonGE_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlstonGE-67">[67]</a></sup> In October 2014, GE announced it was considering the sale of its <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Polish</a> banking business <a href="/wiki/Bank_BPH" title="Bank BPH">Bank BPH</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>Later in 2014, General Electric announced plans to open its global operations center in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>, Ohio.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The Global Operations Center opened in October 2016 as home to GE's multifunctional shared services organization. It supports the company's finance/accounting, human resources, information technology, supply chain, legal and commercial operations, and is one of GE's four multifunctional shared services centers worldwide in <a href="/wiki/Pudong" title="Pudong">Pudong</a>, China; <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, Hungary; and <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2015, GE announced its intention to sell off its property portfolio, worth $26.5 billion, to <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Blackstone_Group" title="The Blackstone Group">The Blackstone Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It was announced in April 2015 that GE would sell most of its finance unit and return around $90 billion to shareholders as the firm looked to trim down on its holdings and rid itself of its image of a "hybrid" company, working in both banking and manufacturing.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In August 2015, GE Capital agreed to sell its Healthcare Financial Services business to <a href="/wiki/Capital_One" title="Capital One">Capital One</a> for US$9 billion. The transaction involved US$8.5 billion of loans made to a wide array of sectors including senior housing, hospitals, medical offices, outpatient services, pharmaceuticals and medical devices.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Also in August 2015, GE Capital agreed to sell GE Capital Bank's on-line deposit platform to <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>. Terms of the transaction were not disclosed, but the sale included US$8 billion of on-line deposits and another US$8 billion of brokered certificates of deposit. The sale was part of GE's strategic plan to exit the U.S. banking sector and to free itself from tightening banking regulations. GE also aimed to shed its status as a "systematically important financial institution".<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2015, GE Capital agreed to sell its transportation-finance unit to Canada's <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Montreal" title="Bank of Montreal">Bank of Montreal</a>. The unit sold had US$8.7 billion (CA$11.5 billion) of assets, 600 employees and 15 offices in the U.S. and Canada. Exact terms of the sale were not disclosed, but the final price would be based on the value of the assets at closing, plus a premium according to the parties.<sup id="cite_ref-GE_Capital_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GE_Capital-75">[75]</a></sup> In October 2015, activist investor <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Peltz" title="Nelson Peltz">Nelson Peltz</a>'s fund Trian bought a $2.5 billion stake in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2016, <a href="/wiki/Haier" title="Haier">Haier</a> Group acquired GE's appliance division for $5.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In October 2016, <a href="/wiki/GE_Renewable_Energy" title="GE Renewable Energy">GE Renewable Energy</a> agreed to pay €1.5 billion to <a href="/wiki/Doughty_Hanson_%26_Co" title="Doughty Hanson &amp; Co">Doughty Hanson &amp; Co</a> for <a href="/wiki/LM_Wind_Power" title="LM Wind Power">LM Wind Power</a> during 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p><p>At the end of October 2016, it was announced that GE was under negotiations for a deal valued at about $30 billion to combine <a href="/wiki/GE_Oil_and_Gas" title="GE Oil and Gas">GE Oil and Gas</a> with <a href="/wiki/Baker_Hughes" title="Baker Hughes">Baker Hughes</a>. The transaction would create a publicly traded entity controlled by GE.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> It was announced that <a href="/wiki/GE_Oil_and_Gas" title="GE Oil and Gas">GE Oil and Gas</a> would sell off its water treatment business as part of its divestment agreement with <a href="/wiki/Baker_Hughes" title="Baker Hughes">Baker Hughes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The deal was cleared by the EU in May 2017, and by the DOJ in June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The merger agreement was approved by shareholders at the end of June 2017. On July 3, 2017, the transaction was completed and Baker Hughes became a GE company and was renamed Bake Hughes, A GE Company (BHGE).<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In November 2018, GE reduced its stake in Baker Hughes to 50.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> On 18 October 2019, GE reduced its stake to 36.8% and the company was renamed back to Baker Hughes.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2017, GE announced the name of their $200 million corporate headquarters would be "GE Innovation Point". The <a href="/wiki/Groundbreaking" title="Groundbreaking">groundbreaking</a> ceremony for the 2.5-acre, 800-person campus was held on May 8, 2017, and the completion date is expected to be sometime in mid-2019.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2017, GE had signed $15 billion of business deals with <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia is one of GE's largest customers.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2017, GE announced the sale of its Industrial Solutions Business to <a href="/wiki/ABB_Group" title="ABB Group">ABB</a>. The deal closed on June 30, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraud_allegations">Fraud allegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Fraud allegations" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On August 15, 2019, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Markopolos" title="Harry Markopolos">Harry Markopolos</a>, a financial fraud investigator known for his discovery of a Ponzi Scheme run by <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Madoff" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernard Madoff">Bernard Madoff</a>, accused General Electric of being a "bigger fraud than Enron", alleging $38 billion in accounting fraud. GE denied wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Insufficient_reserves_for_long-term_care_policies">Insufficient reserves for long-term care policies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Insufficient reserves for long-term care policies" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>It is alleged that GE is "hiding" (i.e. under-reserved) <sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> $29 billion in losses related to its long-term care business.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo_Finance_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo_Finance-96">[96]</a></sup></p><p>According to an August 2019 Fitch Ratings report, there are concerns that GE has not set aside enough money to cover its long-term care liabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018, a lawsuit (the Bezio case) was filed in New York state court on behalf of participants in GE's 401(k) plan and shareowners alleging violations of Section 11 of the <a href="/wiki/Securities_Act_of_1933" title="Securities Act of 1933">Securities Act of 1933</a> based on alleged misstatements and omissions related to insurance reserves and performance of GE's business segments.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p><p>The Kansas Insurance Department (KID) is requiring General Electric to make $14.5 billion of capital contributions for its insurance contracts during the 7-year period ending in 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>  GE reported the total liability related to its insurance contracts was $35.6 billion as at December 31, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018, GE announced the issuance of the new standard by the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) regarding Financial Services - Insurance (Topic 944) will materially affect its financial statements.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>  Mr. Markopolos estimated there will be a $US 10.5 billion charge when the new accounting standard is adopted in the first quarter of 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Anticipated_.248_billion_loss_upon_disposition_of_Baker_Hughes"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Anticipated_$8_billion_loss_upon_disposition_of_Baker_Hughes">Anticipated $8 billion loss upon disposition of Baker Hughes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Anticipated $8 billion loss upon disposition of Baker Hughes" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2017, GE acquired a 62.5% interest in Baker Hughes (BHGE) when it combined its oil &amp; gas business with Baker Hughes Incorporated.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> 
In 2018, GE reduced its interest to 50.4%, resulting in the realization of a $2.1 billion loss.  GE is planning to divest its remaining interest and has warned that the divestment will result in an additional loss of $8.4 billion (assuming a BHGE share price of $23.57 per share).<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In response to the fraud allegations, GE noted the amount of the loss would be $7.4 billion if the divestment occurred on July 26, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>  Mr. Markopolos noted that BHGE is an asset available for sale and therefore <a href="/wiki/Mark-to-market_accounting" title="Mark-to-market accounting">mark-to-market accounting</a> is required.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_ratio_of_0.67">Current ratio of 0.67</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Current ratio of 0.67" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Mr. Markopolos noted GE's <a href="/wiki/Current_ratio" title="Current ratio">current ratio</a> was only 0.67.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo_Finance_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo_Finance-96">[96]</a></sup> He expressed concerns that GE may file for bankruptcy if there is a recession.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2018, the GE Pension Plan reported losses of $US 3.3 billion on plan assets.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p><p>In 2018, General Electric changed the discount rate used to calculate the actuarial liabilities of its pension plans.  The rate was increased from 3.64% to 4.34%.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-110">[110]</a></sup>  Consequently, the reported liability for the underfunded pension plans decreased by $7 billion year-over-year, from $34.2 billion in 2017 to $27.2 billion in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-110">[110]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2018, General Electric announced it would "freeze pensions" for about 20,000 salaried U.S. employees.  The employees will be moved to a defined-contribution retirement plan in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><p>On March 30th, 2020, General Electric factory workers protested to convert jet engine factories to make ventilators during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" class="mw-redirect" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a> crisis. <sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_performance">Financial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Financial performance" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">

</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Dividends">Dividends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Dividends" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2018, GE reduced its quarterly dividend from $0.12 to $0.01 per share.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Stock">Stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Stock" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>As a publicly-traded company on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>, GE stock was one of the 30 components of the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> from 1907 to 2018, the longest continuous presence of any company on the index, and during this time the only company which was part of the original Dow Jones Industrial Index created in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-fact_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fact-127">[127]</a></sup> On June 26, 2018, the stock was removed from the index and replaced with <a href="/wiki/Walgreens_Boots_Alliance" title="Walgreens Boots Alliance">Walgreens Boots Alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In the years leading to its removal, GE was the worst performing stock in the Dow, falling more than 55 percent <a href="/wiki/Year_on_year" title="Year on year">year on year</a> and more than 25 percent <a href="/wiki/Year_to_date" class="mw-redirect" title="Year to date">year to date</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed"><li class="gallerybox" style="width: 178.66666666667px"><div style="width: 178.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 176.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Linear_GE_Stock_Price_Graph_1962-2013.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Linear_GE_Stock_Price_Graph_1962-2013.png/265px-Linear_GE_Stock_Price_Graph_1962-2013.png" decoding="async" width="177" height="120" data-file-width="1408" data-file-height="958"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 177px;height: 120px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Linear_GE_Stock_Price_Graph_1962-2013.png/265px-Linear_GE_Stock_Price_Graph_1962-2013.png" data-alt="" data-width="177" data-height="120"> </span></a></div></div>

		</div></li>
</ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Bribery">Bribery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Bribery" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>In July 2010, General Electric was willing to pay $23.4 million to settle an SEC complaint, as GE bribed Iraqi government officials to win contracts under the U.N. oil-for-food program. 
<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GeneralElectricSign.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/GeneralElectricSign.jpg/220px-GeneralElectricSign.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2029" data-file-height="2000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 217px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/GeneralElectricSign.jpg/220px-GeneralElectricSign.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="217" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GeneralElectricSign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A General Electric <a href="/wiki/Neon_sign" title="Neon sign">neon sign</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1959, General Electric was accused of promoting the largest illegal cartel in the United States since the adoption of the Sherman Antitrust Act. (1890) in order to maintain artificially high prices. In total, 29 companies and 45 executives will be convicted. Subsequent parliamentary inquiries revealed that "white-collar crime" was by far the most costly form of crime for the United States' finances.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p><p>GE is a multinational conglomerate headquartered in Boston, Massachusetts.<sup id="cite_ref-10K2017_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K2017-132">[132]</a></sup> However its main offices are located at <a href="/wiki/30_Rockefeller_Plaza" title="30 Rockefeller Plaza">30 Rockefeller Plaza</a> at <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, known now as the Comcast Building.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (May 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> It was formerly known as the GE Building for the prominent GE logo on the roof; <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s headquarters and main studios are also located in the building. Through its RCA subsidiary, it has been associated with the center since its construction in the 1930s. GE moved its corporate headquarters from the GE Building on Lexington Avenue to <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_Connecticut" title="Fairfield, Connecticut">Fairfield, Connecticut</a> in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In 2016, GE announced a move to the <a href="/wiki/South_Boston_Waterfront" class="mw-redirect" title="South Boston Waterfront">South Boston Waterfront</a> neighborhood of Boston, Massachusetts, partly as a result of an incentive package provide by state and city governments. The first group of workers arrived in the summer of 2016, and the full move will be completed by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (February 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> Due to poor financial performance and corporate downsizing, GE sold the land it planned to build its new headquarters building on, instead choosing to occupy neighboring leased buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p><p>GE's tax return is the largest return filed in the United States; the 2005 return was approximately 24,000 pages when printed out, and 237 megabytes when submitted electronically.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The company also "spends more on U.S. <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a> than any other company".<sup id="cite_ref-Carney_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carney-140">[140]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, GE launched its "<i>Ecomagination</i>" initiative in an attempt to position itself as a "green" company.
GE is one of the biggest players in the wind power industry, and is developing environment-friendly products such as hybrid locomotives, desalination and water reuse solutions, and photovoltaic cells. The company "plans to build the largest solar-panel-making factory in the U.S.,"<sup id="cite_ref-Carney_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carney-140">[140]</a></sup> and has set goals for its subsidiaries to lower their greenhouse gas emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p><p>On May 21, 2007, GE announced it would sell its GE Plastics division to petrochemicals manufacturer SABIC for net proceeds of $11.6 billion. The transaction took place on August 31, 2007, and the company name changed to SABIC Innovative Plastics, with Brian Gladden as CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2017, GE announced that the company intends to close the <a href="/wiki/Gender_pay_gap" title="Gender pay gap">gender gap</a> by promising to hire and place 20,000 women in technical roles by 2020. The company is also seeking to have a 50:50 male to female <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender representation</a> in all <a href="/wiki/Entry-level" class="mw-redirect" title="Entry-level">entry-level</a> technical programs.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2017, GE announced they would be closing research and development centers in Shanghai, Munich and Rio de Janeiro. The company spent $5 billion on R&amp;D in the last year.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p><p>On February 25, 2019, GE sold its diesel locomotive business to <a href="/wiki/Westinghouse_Air_Brake_Technologies_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Westinghouse Air Brake Technologies Corporation">Westinghouse Air Brake Technologies Corporation</a> (WAB), also known as <a href="/wiki/Wabtec" class="mw-redirect" title="Wabtec">Wabtec</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="CEO">CEO</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: CEO" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of October 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/John_L._Flannery" title="John L. Flannery">John L. Flannery</a> was replaced by <a href="/wiki/H._Lawrence_Culp_Jr." title="H. Lawrence Culp Jr.">H. Lawrence Culp Jr.</a> as Chairman and CEO in a unanimous vote of the GE Board of Directors.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/John_L._Flannery" title="John L. Flannery">John L. Flannery</a> had succeeded <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_R._Immelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeffrey R. Immelt">Jeffrey Immelt</a> as chief executive officer and chairman of the board of GE.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_A._Coffin" title="Charles A. Coffin">Charles A. Coffin</a> (1913–1922)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Owen_D._Young" title="Owen D. Young">Owen D. Young</a> (1922–1939, 1942–1945)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Philip_D._Reed" title="Philip D. Reed">Philip D. Reed</a> (1940–1942, 1945–1958)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ralph_J._Cordiner" title="Ralph J. Cordiner">Ralph J. Cordiner</a> (1958–1963)</li>
<li>Gerald L. Phillippe (1963–1972)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fred_J._Borch" title="Fred J. Borch">Fred J. Borch</a> (1967–1972)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reginald_H._Jones" title="Reginald H. Jones">Reginald H. Jones</a> (1972–1981)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jack_Welch" title="Jack Welch">Jack Welch</a> (1981–2001)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Immelt" title="Jeff Immelt">Jeff Immelt</a> (2001–2017)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Flannery" class="mw-disambig" title="John Flannery">John Flannery</a> (2017–2018)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/H._Lawrence_Culp_Jr." title="H. Lawrence Culp Jr.">H. Lawrence Culp Jr.</a> (2018–present)</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_recognition_and_rankings">Corporate recognition and rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Corporate recognition and rankings" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> ranked GE the sixth-largest firm in the U.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_500:_GE_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_500:_GE-148">[148]</a></sup> and the 14th-most profitable.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_500:_IBM_profit_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_500:_IBM_profit-7">[7]</a></sup> Other rankings for 2011/2012 include the following:<sup id="cite_ref-Fast_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fast-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>#18 company for leaders (<i>Fortune</i>)</li>
<li>#6 best global brand (<i><a href="/wiki/Interbrand" title="Interbrand">Interbrand</a></i>)</li>
<li>#82 green company (<i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>)</li>
<li>#91 most admired company (<i>Fortune</i>)</li>
<li>#19 most innovative company (<i><a href="/wiki/Fast_Company_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fast Company (magazine)">Fast Company</a></i>).</li></ul><p>In 2012, GE's brand was valued at $28.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> CEO <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Immelt" title="Jeff Immelt">Jeff Immelt</a> had a set of changes in the presentation of the brand commissioned in 2004, after he took the reins as chairman, to unify the diversified businesses of GE.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The changes included a new corporate color palette, small modifications to the GE logo, a new customized font (GE Inspira) and a new slogan, "Imagination at work", composed by David Lucas, to replace the slogan "<a href="/wiki/We_Bring_Good_Things_to_Life" title="We Bring Good Things to Life">We Bring Good Things to Life</a>" used since 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-slogan_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slogan-151">[151]</a></sup> The standard requires many headlines to be lowercased and adds visual "white space" to documents and advertising. The changes were designed by <a href="/wiki/Wolff_Olins" title="Wolff Olins">Wolff Olins</a> and are used on GE's marketing, literature and website. In 2014, a second typeface family was introduced: GE Sans and Serif by Bold Monday created under art direction by Wolff Olins.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, GE had appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list for 22 years and held the 11th rank.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> GE was removed from the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> on June 28, 2018, after the value had dropped below 1% of the index's weight.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
