</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Businesses">Businesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Businesses" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_General_Electric" title="List of assets owned by General Electric">List of assets owned by General Electric</a></div>
<p>GE's primary business divisions are:
</p>
<ul><li>GE Additive</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Aviation" title="GE Aviation">GE Aviation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Capital" title="GE Capital">GE Capital</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Digital" title="GE Digital">GE Digital</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Healthcare" title="GE Healthcare">GE Healthcare</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Lighting" title="GE Lighting">GE Lighting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Power" title="GE Power">GE Power</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Renewable_Energy" title="GE Renewable Energy">GE Renewable Energy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GE_Global_Research" title="GE Global Research">GE Global Research</a></li></ul><p>The former <a href="/wiki/GE_Transportation" title="GE Transportation">GE Transportation</a> division merged with <a href="/wiki/Wabtec_Corporation" title="Wabtec Corporation">Wabtec</a> on February 25, 2019, leaving GE with a 24.9% holding in Wabtec.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p><p>The former <a href="/wiki/GE_Home_%26_Business_Solutions" title="GE Home &amp; Business Solutions">GE Appliances and Lighting</a> segment was dissolved in 2014 when GE's appliance division was sold to <a href="/wiki/Haier" title="Haier">Haier</a> for $5.4 billion. <a href="/wiki/GE_Lighting" title="GE Lighting">GE Lighting</a> (consumer lighting) and the newly created <a href="/wiki/Current_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Current (company)">Current, powered by GE</a>, which deals in commercial LED, solar, EV, and energy storage, became stand-alone businesses within the company,<sup id="cite_ref-cnetHaier_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnetHaier-156">[156]</a></sup> until the sale of the later to American Industrial Partners in April 2019<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p><p>Through these businesses, GE participates in markets that include the generation, transmission and distribution of electricity (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear reactor technology">nuclear</a>, gas and solar), <a href="/wiki/Lighting" title="Lighting">lighting</a>, industrial <a href="/wiki/Automation" title="Automation">automation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging" title="Medical imaging">medical imaging</a> equipment, motors, <a href="/wiki/Locomotive" title="Locomotive">railway locomotives</a>, aircraft jet engines, and aviation services. Through GE Commercial Finance, GE Consumer Finance, GE Equipment Services, and GE Insurance it offers a range of financial services. It has a presence in over 100 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LocomotiveGaugesSRM.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/LocomotiveGaugesSRM.jpg/220px-LocomotiveGaugesSRM.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/LocomotiveGaugesSRM.jpg/220px-LocomotiveGaugesSRM.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LocomotiveGaugesSRM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GE gauges to control a railway <a href="/wiki/Locomotive" title="Locomotive">locomotive</a> at a museum near <a href="/wiki/Saskatoon" title="Saskatoon">Saskatoon</a>, Canada<sup id="cite_ref-SRM_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRM-159">[159]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>General Imaging manufacturers GE digital cameras.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p><p>Even though the first wave of conglomerates (such as <a href="/wiki/ITT_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="ITT Corporation">ITT Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ling-Temco-Vought" title="Ling-Temco-Vought">Ling-Temco-Vought</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenneco" title="Tenneco">Tenneco</a>, etc.) fell by the wayside by the mid-1980s, in the late 1990s, another wave (consisting of <a href="/wiki/Westinghouse_Electric_(1886)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westinghouse Electric (1886)">Westinghouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyco_International" title="Tyco International">Tyco</a>, and others) tried and failed to emulate GE's success.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p><p>On May 4, 2008, it was announced that GE would auction off its appliances business for an expected sale of $5–8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> However, this plan fell through as a result of the recession.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p><p>As of August 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> GE is planning to set up a <a href="/wiki/Silicon_carbide" title="Silicon carbide">silicon carbide</a> chip packaging R&amp;D center in coalition with <a href="/wiki/SUNY_Polytechnic_Institute" title="SUNY Polytechnic Institute">SUNY Polytechnic Institute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Utica,_New_York" title="Utica, New York">Utica, New York</a>. The project will create 470 jobs with the potential to grow to 820 jobs within 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p><p>On September 14, 2015, GE announced the creation of a new unit: GE Digital, which will bring together its software and IT capabilities. The new business unit will be headed by Bill Ruh, who joined GE in 2011 from Cisco Systems and has since worked on GE's software efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Environmental record" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution">Pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Pollution" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>GE has a history of some of its activities giving rise to large-scale <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>. Based on data from 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> researchers at the Political Economy Research Institute listed the corporation as the fourth-largest corporate producer of <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_the_United_States" title="Air pollution in the United States">air pollution in the United States</a>, with more than 4.4 million pounds per year (2,000 tons) of toxic chemicals released into the air.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> GE has also been implicated in the creation of <a href="/wiki/Toxic_waste" title="Toxic waste">toxic waste</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a> documents, only the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Government">United States Government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron Corporation</a> are responsible for producing more <a href="/wiki/Superfund" title="Superfund">Superfund</a> toxic waste sites.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p><p>In 1983, <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Attorney_General" class="mw-redirect" title="New York State Attorney General">New York State Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Abrams" title="Robert Abrams">Robert Abrams</a> filed suit in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_New_York" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of New York">United States District Court for the Northern District of New York</a> to compel GE to pay for the clean-up of what was claimed to be more than 100,000 tons of chemicals dumped from their plant in <a href="/wiki/Waterford,_New_York" title="Waterford, New York">Waterford, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> In 1999, the company agreed to pay a $250 million settlement in connection with claims it polluted the <a href="/wiki/Housatonic_River" title="Housatonic River">Housatonic River</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pittsfield,_Massachusetts" title="Pittsfield, Massachusetts">Pittsfield, Massachusetts</a>) and other sites with <a href="/wiki/Polychlorinated_biphenyl" title="Polychlorinated biphenyl">polychlorinated biphenyls</a> (PCBs) and other hazardous substances.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p><p>In 2003, acting on concerns that the plan proposed by GE did not "provide for adequate protection of public health and the environment," the United States Environmental Protection Agency issued a unilateral administrative order for the company to "address cleanup at the GE site" in <a href="/wiki/Rome,_Georgia" title="Rome, Georgia">Rome, Georgia</a>, also contaminated with PCBs.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactors</a> involved in the 2011 crisis at <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant">Fukushima I</a> in Japan were GE designs,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> and the architectural designs were done by <a href="/wiki/Ebasco" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebasco">Ebasco</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> formerly owned by GE. Concerns over the design and safety of these reactors were raised as early as 1972, but <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a> danger was not discussed at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the same model nuclear power reactors designed by GE are operating in the US,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> however, as of May 31, 2019, the controversial <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_Nuclear_Generating_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim Nuclear Generating Station">Pilgrim Nuclear Generating Station</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth, Massachusetts">Plymouth, Massachusetts</a>, has been shutdown and is in the process of decommission.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution_of_the_Hudson_River">Pollution of the Hudson River</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Pollution of the Hudson River" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pollution_of_the_Hudson_River" title="Pollution of the Hudson River">Pollution of the Hudson River</a></div>
<p>GE heavily contaminated the Hudson River with <a href="/wiki/Polychlorinated_biphenyl" title="Polychlorinated biphenyl">polychlorinated biphenyls (PCBs)</a> between 1947 and 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-epa_ge_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epa_ge-176">[176]</a></sup> This pollution caused a range of harmful effects to wildlife and people who eat fish from the river or drink the water.<sup id="cite_ref-epa_gel_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epa_gel-177">[177]</a></sup> In response to the contamination, activists protested in various ways. Musician <a href="/wiki/Pete_Seeger" title="Pete Seeger">Pete Seeger</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River_Sloop_Clearwater" title="Hudson River Sloop Clearwater">Hudson River Sloop Clearwater</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Clearwater_Festival" title="Clearwater Festival">Clearwater Festival</a> to draw attention to the problem. In 1983, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a> (EPA) declared a 200-mile (320 km) stretch of the river, from Hudson Falls to New York City, to be a <a href="/wiki/Superfund" title="Superfund">Superfund</a> site requiring cleanup. This Superfund site is considered to be one of the largest in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-upi.com_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upi.com-178">[178]</a></sup> Other sources of pollution, including mercury contamination and sewage dumping, have also contributed to problems in the Hudson River watershed.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoD3-29_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoD3-29-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nysdec_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nysdec-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution_of_the_Housatonic_River">Pollution of the Housatonic River</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Pollution of the Housatonic River" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>From <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1932</span> until 1977, GE polluted the <a href="/wiki/Housatonic_River" title="Housatonic River">Housatonic River</a> with PCB discharges from its plant at <a href="/wiki/Pittsfield,_Massachusetts" title="Pittsfield, Massachusetts">Pittsfield, Massachusetts</a>. EPA designated the Pittsfield plant and several miles of the Housatonic to be a Superfund site in 1997, and ordered GE to remediate the site.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Aroclor 1254 and Aroclor 1260, made by <a href="/wiki/Monsanto" title="Monsanto">Monsanto</a> was the primary contaminant of the pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-183">[183]</a></sup> The highest concentrations of PCBs in the Housatonic River are found in Woods Pond in <a href="/wiki/Lenox,_Massachusetts" title="Lenox, Massachusetts">Lenox, Massachusetts</a>, just south of Pittsfield, where they have been measured up to 110 mg/kg in the sediment.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-183">[183]</a></sup> About 50% of all the PCBs currently in the river are estimated to be retained in the sediment behind Woods Pond dam. This is estimated to be about 11,000 pounds (5,000 kg) of PCBs.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_183-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-183">[183]</a></sup> Former filled oxbows are also polluted.<sup id="cite_ref-EPA1_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPA1-184">[184]</a></sup> Waterfowl and fish who live in and around the river contain significant levels of PCBs and can present health risks if consumed.<sup id="cite_ref-CTDPH1_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CTDPH1-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MDPH_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MDPH-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_initiatives">Environmental initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Environmental initiatives" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GE_Schenectady.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GE_Schenectady.JPG/220px-GE_Schenectady.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GE_Schenectady.JPG/220px-GE_Schenectady.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GE_Schenectady.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GE facility in <a href="/wiki/Schenectady,_New_York" title="Schenectady, New York">Schenectady, New York</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EVChargingMarkham.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/EVChargingMarkham.jpg/170px-EVChargingMarkham.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 257px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/EVChargingMarkham.jpg/170px-EVChargingMarkham.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="257" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EVChargingMarkham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A General Electric EV charging station in North America</div></div></div>
<p>On June 6, 2011, GE announced that it has licensed solar thermal technology from California-based eSolar for use in power plants that use both solar and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p><p>On May 26, 2011, GE unveiled its EV Solar Carport, a <a href="/wiki/Carport" title="Carport">carport</a> that incorporates solar panels on its roof, with electric vehicle charging stations under its cover.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2005, GE announced the launch of a program called "Ecomagination", intended, in the words of CEO Jeff Immelt, "to develop tomorrow's solutions such as solar energy, hybrid locomotives, fuel cells, lower-emission aircraft engines, lighter and stronger durable materials, efficient lighting, and water purification technology".<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> The announcement prompted an op-ed piece in <i>The New York Times</i> to observe that, "while General Electric's increased emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Clean_technology" title="Clean technology">clean technology</a> will probably result in improved products and benefit its bottom line, Mr. Immelt's credibility as a spokesman on national environmental policy is fatally flawed because of his company's intransigence in cleaning up its own toxic legacy."<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p><p>GE has said that it will invest $1.4 billion in clean technology research and development in 2008 as part of its Ecomagination initiative. As of October 2008, the scheme had resulted in 70 green products being brought to market, ranging from halogen lamps to biogas engines. In 2007, GE raised the annual revenue target for its Ecomagination initiative from $20 billion in 2010 to $25 billion following positive market response to its new product lines.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> In 2010, GE continued to raise its investment by adding $10 billion into Ecomagination over the next five years.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p><p>GE Energy's <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> business has expanded greatly, to keep up with growing U.S. and global demand for <a href="/wiki/Clean_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Clean energy">clean energy</a>. Since entering the <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_industry" title="Renewable energy industry">renewable energy industry</a> in 2002, GE has invested more than $850 million in <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialization" title="Renewable energy commercialization">renewable energy commercialization</a>. In August 2008 it acquired Kelman Ltd,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> a Northern Ireland-based company specializing in advanced monitoring and diagnostics technologies for transformers used in renewable energy generation, and announced an expansion of its business in Northern Ireland in May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> In 2009, GE's renewable energy initiatives, which include <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> and <a href="/wiki/GE_Jenbacher" class="mw-redirect" title="GE Jenbacher">GE Jenbacher</a> <a href="/wiki/Gas_engines" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas engines">gas engines</a> using renewable and non-renewable methane-based gases,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> employ more than 4,900 people globally and have created more than 10,000 supporting jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p><p>GE Energy and <a href="/wiki/Orion_New_Zealand_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Orion New Zealand Limited">Orion New Zealand Limited</a> (Orion) have announced implementation of the first phase of a GE network management system to help improve power reliability for customers. GE's ENMAC Distribution Management System is the foundation of Orion's initiative. The system of <a href="/wiki/Smart_grid" title="Smart grid">smart grid</a> technologies will significantly improve the network company's ability to manage big network emergencies and help it to restore power faster when outages occur.
</p><p>In June 2018, GE Volunteers, an internal group of GE Employees, along with Malaysian Nature Society transplanted more than 270 plants from the Taman Tugu forest reserve so that they may be replanted in the forest trail which is under construction.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational_initiatives">Educational initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Educational initiatives" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>GE Healthcare is collaborating with The <a href="/wiki/Wayne_State_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Wayne State University School of Medicine">Wayne State University School of Medicine</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Medical_University_of_South_Carolina" title="Medical University of South Carolina">Medical University of South Carolina</a> to offer an integrated radiology curriculum during their respective MD Programs led by investigators of the <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Diagnostic_Ultrasound_in_micro-gravity" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Diagnostic Ultrasound in micro-gravity">Advanced Diagnostic Ultrasound in micro-gravity</a> study.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> GE has donated over one million dollars of Logiq E Ultrasound equipment to these two institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_initiatives">Marketing initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Marketing initiatives" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2011.E2.80.932013_content-marketing_campaigns"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2013_content-marketing_campaigns">2011–2013 content-marketing campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 2011–2013 content-marketing campaigns" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Between September 2011 and April 2013, GE ran a <a href="/wiki/Content_marketing" title="Content marketing">content marketing</a> campaign dedicated to telling the stories of "innovators—people who are reshaping the world through act or invention". The initiative included 30 3-minute films from leading documentary film directors (<a href="/wiki/Albert_and_David_Maysles" title="Albert and David Maysles">Albert Maysles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Yu" title="Jessica Yu">Jessica Yu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Iwerks" title="Leslie Iwerks">Leslie Iwerks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_James_(producer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Steve James (producer)">Steve James</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Gibney" title="Alex Gibney">Alex Gibney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lixin_Fan" title="Lixin Fan">Lixin Fan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Hustwit" title="Gary Hustwit">Gary Hustwit</a> and others), and a user-generated competition that received over 600 submissions, out of which 20 finalists were chosen.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup></p><p><i>Short Films, Big Ideas</i> was launched at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a> in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Spurlock" title="Morgan Spurlock">cinelan</a>. Stories included breakthroughs in <a href="/wiki/Water_treatment" title="Water treatment">Slingshot (water vapor distillation system)</a>, cancer research, energy production, pain management and food access. Each of the 30 films received world premiere screenings at a major international film festival, including the <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a>. The winning amateur director film, <i>The Cyborg Foundation</i>, was awarded a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$100,000</span> prize at the 2013 at Sundance Film Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> According to GE, the campaign garnered more than 1.5 billion total media impressions, 14 million online views, and was seen in 156 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sponsorships" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Theater" title="General Electric Theater">General Electric Theater</a></div>
<p>In January 2017, GE signed an estimated $7 million deal with the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a> to have its corporate logo put on the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> team's jersey.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_affiliation">Political affiliation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Political affiliation" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<p>In the 1950s GE sponsored <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Theater" title="General Electric Theater">TV career</a> and launched him on the lecture circuit. GE's has also designed social programs, supported civil rights organizations, and funds minority education programs.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_appearances_in_media">Notable appearances in media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notable appearances in media" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<p>In the early 1950s <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Vonnegut" title="Kurt Vonnegut">Kurt Vonnegut</a> was a writer for GE. A number of his novels and stories (notably <i><a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_Cradle" title="Cat's Cradle">Cat's Cradle</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Player_Piano_(novel)" title="Player Piano (novel)">Player Piano</a></i>) refer to the fictional city of <a href="/wiki/Ilium_(Kurt_Vonnegut)" title="Ilium (Kurt Vonnegut)">Ilium</a>, which appears to be loosely based on Schenectady, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The Ilium Works is the setting for the short story "<a href="/wiki/Deer_in_the_Works" title="Deer in the Works">Deer in the Works</a>".
</p><p>In 1981, GE won a <a href="/wiki/Clio_award" class="mw-redirect" title="Clio award">Clio award</a> for its :30 Soft White Light Bulbs commercial, <a href="/wiki/We_Bring_Good_Things_to_Life" title="We Bring Good Things to Life">We Bring Good Things to Life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> The slogan "We Bring Good Things to Life" was created by <a href="/wiki/Phil_Dusenberry" title="Phil Dusenberry">Phil Dusenberry</a> at the ad agency <a href="/wiki/BBDO" title="BBDO">BBDO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p><p>GE was the primary focus of a 1991 short subject <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>-winning documentary, <i>Deadly Deception: General Electric, Nuclear Weapons, and Our Environment</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> that juxtaposed GE's "We Bring Good Things To Life" commercials with the true stories of workers and neighbors whose lives have been affected by the company's activities involving <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p><p>In 2013, GE received a National <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Awards_for_Public_Service" title="Jefferson Awards for Public Service">Jefferson Award</a> for Outstanding Service by a Major Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Electric&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">

<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-102">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ge.com/investor-relations/sites/default/files/ge_webcast_10Q_10302018.pdf">"FORM 10-Q September 2018"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>GE.com</i>. General Ledger. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190820235127/https://www.ge.com/investor-relations/sites/default/files/ge_webcast_10Q_10302018.pdf">Archived</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> from the original on August 20, 2019<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 21,</span> 2019</span>. <q>In August 2018, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued Accounting Standards Update (ASU) No. 2018-12, Financial Services - Insurance (Topic 944): Targeted Improvements to the Accounting for Long-Duration Contracts. We are evaluating the effect of the standard on our consolidated financial statements and anticipate that its adoption will significantly change the accounting for measurements of our long-duration insurance liabilities. The ASU requires cash flow assumptions used in the measurement of various insurance liabilities to be reviewed at least annually and updated if actual experience or other evidence indicates previous assumptions need to be revised with any required changes recorded in earnings. The discount rate, equivalent to the upper-medium grade (i.e., single A) fixed-income instrument yield reflecting the duration characteristics of the liability, is required to be updated in each reporting period with changes recorded in accumulated other comprehensive income. In measuring the insurance liabilities, contracts shall not be grouped together from different issue years. While we continue to evaluate the effect of the standard on our ongoing financial reporting, we anticipate that the adoption of the ASU may materially affect our financial statements.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=GE.com&amp;rft.atitle=FORM+10-Q+September+2018&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ge.com%2Finvestor-relations%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2Fge_webcast_10Q_10302018.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGeneral+Electric" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">General Electric. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ge.com/investor-relations/sites/default/files/GE_AR18.pdf">"2018 Annual Report - General Electric"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>GE.com</i>. p. 139. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190923162718/https://www.ge.com/investor-relations/sites/default/files/GE_AR18.pdf">Archived</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> from the original on September 23, 2019<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 20,</span> 2019</span>. <q>As previously announced, we plan an orderly separation of our ownership interest in BHGE over time. In November 2018, BHGE completed an underwritten public offering in which we sold 101.2 million shares of BHGE Class A common stock. BHGE also repurchased 65.0 million BHGE LLC units from GE. As a result, our economic interest in BHGE reduced from 62.5% to 50.4% and we recognized a loss of $2,169 million ($1,696 million after tax), which decreased the Other Capital component of shareowners' equity. Sale of Class A common stock resulted in an increase in noncontrolling interests of $4,214 million. Any reduction in our ownership interest below 50% will result in us losing control of BHGE. At that point, we would deconsolidate our Oil &amp; Gas segment, recognize any remaining interest at fair value and recognize any difference between carrying value and fair value of our interest in earnings. Depending on the form and timing of our separation, and if BHGE’s stock price remains below our current carrying value, we may recognize a significant loss in earnings. Based on BHGE's share price at January 31, 2019 of $23.57 per share, the incremental loss upon deconsolidation by a sale of our interest would be approximately $8,400 million.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=GE.com&amp;rft.atitle=2018+Annual+Report+-+General+Electric&amp;rft.pages=139&amp;rft.au=General+Electric&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ge.com%2Finvestor-relations%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2FGE_AR18.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGeneral+Electric" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
